    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer18174059621384603011">In Colombia you have to pick a side. Or one will be picked for you . . .<br/><br/>All Pedro GutiÃ©rrez cares about is fishing, playing pool and his girlfriend Camilaâs promise to sleep with him on his sixteenth birthday.   <span id="freeText18174059621384603011" style="display:none">In Colombia you have to pick a side. Or one will be picked for you . . .<br /><br />All Pedro GutiÃ©rrez cares about is fishing, playing pool and his girlfriend Camilaâs promise to sleep with him on his sixteenth birthday. But his life is ripped apart when Guerrilla soldiers callously execute his father in front of him, and he and his mother are banished from their farm.<br /><br />Swearing vengeance against the five men responsible, Pedro, with his best friend Palillo, joins an illegal Paramilitary group, where he is trained to fight, kill and crush any sign of weakness.<br /><br />But as he descends into a world of unspeakable violence, Pedro must decide how far he is willing to go. Can he stop himself before he becomes just as ruthless as those he is hunting? Or will his dark obsession cost him all he loves?<br /><br />Colombiano is an epic tale of rural villages held to ransom, of jungle drug labs, cocaine supermarkets, witch doctors and buried millions, of innocent teenage love, barbaric torture and meticulously planned revenge.<br /><br />Superbly told and by turns gripping, poignant and darkly comic, Colombiano is the remarkable story of a boy whose moral descent becomes a metaphor for the corruption of an entire nation. Both blockbuster thriller and electrifying coming-of-age story, Rusty Youngâs powerful novel is also a meditation on the redeeming power of love.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16865130745265367741">â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ <br/><br/>Wow! What a powerful story this is, depicting as it does the conflict between the army and opposing Guerrilla groups in Colombia, and in particular it features the child soldiers who were either forced into joining these groups or had very good reason for committing their lives to such a violent cause. Though fictional, author Rusty Youngâs Colombiano is based on interviews that he conducted with child soldiers, and he draws on his own life experiences too, having worked undercove</span>
  <span id="freeText16865130745265367741" style="display:none">â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ â­ï¸ <br /><br />Wow! What a powerful story this is, depicting as it does the conflict between the army and opposing Guerrilla groups in Colombia, and in particular it features the child soldiers who were either forced into joining these groups or had very good reason for committing their lives to such a violent cause. Though fictional, author Rusty Youngâs Colombiano is based on interviews that he conducted with child soldiers, and he draws on his own life experiences too, having worked undercover for the US government in counter terrorism - those facts alone make this such a chilling yet utterly compelling read!<br /><br />15 year old Pedro GutiÃ©rrez is a farmerâs son, he loves helping his dad around the farm, and hopes to inherit it some day. He relishes the time he and his father spend fishing too, though equally he enjoys playing pool with his friends, and he also loves his girlfriend Camila. Heâs just an ordinary boy doing ordinary things, and heâs really happy with his life, but all that changes when his beloved father is executed in front of him by Guerilla soldiers - not only that, but he and his mother are banished from their farm, which leaves them without an income. Pedro swears he will find every one of those soldiers involved, and promises to avenge his fatherâs death, so, together with his best friend Palillo, he joins an illegal Paramilitary black ops organisation. The training is tough, ruthless and violent, but it turns him into the killer that he needs to be in order to carry out his promise.<br /><br />We follow Pedro as he rises through the ranks, and experience the heart stopping missions that he takes part in, and of course his relationship with Camila is always there in the background, but itâs his determination to kill those who took part in his fatherâs death that takes centre stage.<br /><br />At almost 700 pages, this isnât a short read, but donât let that put you off, I couldnât put it down and literally raced through it, and the fact that the chapters are bite sized certainly helped.<br /><br />What can I say to explain how excellent this book was? Iâll admit that parts of it were really difficult to read due to the level of violence - itâs horrifying just what these child soldiers were made to participate in, but I became 100% emotionally involved in this fast paced and thrilling ride through Colombiaâs darkest days. From first page to last, this is, without question, exceptional, and undoubtedly one of the best books that Iâve read this year!<br /><br />* My thanks to Lily Green at Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing, and to author Rusty Young for my signed copy of Colombiano. I have given an honest unbiased review in exchange *</span>

<div id="review_2376788560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376788560" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376788560?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376788560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14642094452510366037"><b>Animosity</b><br/>A book that's packed with a real right-hook. I expected a documentary-style book outlining the research and feedback Rusty Young had gathered from the many interviews and investigations he had undertaken in the region, especially with the real-life Child Soldiers. Not the case!<br/><br/><i>Colombiano</i> is a novel styled book which is cleverly written, it is engrossing and absorbing with shocking revelations. The story is based on a fictional character, Pedro (probably an amalgamation of several people</span>
  <span id="freeText14642094452510366037" style="display:none"><b>Animosity</b><br />A book that's packed with a real right-hook. I expected a documentary-style book outlining the research and feedback Rusty Young had gathered from the many interviews and investigations he had undertaken in the region, especially with the real-life Child Soldiers. Not the case!<br /><br /><i>Colombiano</i> is a novel styled book which is cleverly written, it is engrossing and absorbing with shocking revelations. The story is based on a fictional character, Pedro (probably an amalgamation of several people in an attempt to protect identities), who experiences the events that drove him to enrol as a child soldier and fight in a conflict that was brutal, remorseless, perilous and full of hate. <br /><br />Law and order do not exist in the traditional sense in Colombia. During their troubled past, there have been a number of factions. Firstly the <i>Colombian Army</i> and police forces providing limited law and order in a divided country â not to mention their exposure to corruption and criminality. The second group was the <i>FARC Guerrilla</i>, who were peasant farmers who took up arms, aiming to fight poverty and social inequality by toppling the government and installing communist rule. To fund their revolution, they âtaxedâ businesses and kidnapped the rich, appropriating their lands for redistribution to the poor. The third group were the <i>Paramilitaries</i> who were wealthy land and business owners, tired of the governmentâs failure to protect them, who formed their own private militias and âdeath squadsâ. <blockquote>
  <i> âNo matter how hard you try, you canât remain neutral. Eventually, you have to pick a side. And if you donât, one will be picked for you. As it was for me.â</i>
</blockquote><br />When Pedro was 15 years old he had to witness his father being executed by the Guerrilla for allowing the army to drink their water on the farm. There may have been other reasons and often it was to send a message. The execution is cold and clinical but disturbingly they are not allowed to bury the body in the consecrated ground and have a priest pray for his soul. While Pedroâs parents had always pleaded with him to remain neutral, now his fatherâs death must be avenged.<br /><br />Rusty Young creates excellent characters, particular, Pedro, and a society that is circumspect and threated by cruelty from forces on all sides. He portrays an environment where the futility of staying removed from the violence is common, where events can strike and change a life in a matter of moments, and where hate and revenge are the staple diet of young men and women. Who can say what we would do if we watched a family member murdered and the law enforcement unwilling or unable to address the crime? Unfortunately, bloodshed begets bloodshed and when all sides can cite atrocities the spiral into horror and hostility is the norm.<br /><br />The length of the book is nearly 700 pages and I started it with the decision in my mind that if this dragged I would stop and not commit any more time to a book I wasnât enjoying. I read the 689 pages and also read other material around the subject. An advantage in reading this book is that the chapters are short and progression is easy to sustain. I felt the writing was excellent and the pace of the book was brilliantly maintained creating a totally enthralling story.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book and I would like to thank Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and NetGalley for providing me with an ARC version in return for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14642094452510366037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kylie D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80033559-kylie-d"><img alt="Kylie D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527289322p2/80033559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734021622?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kylie D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kylie D" href="/user/show/80033559-kylie-d">Kylie D</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43861960-colombiano">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=atwi80b-2019">atwi80b-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=annual-challenges">annual-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=netgalley-2019">netgalley-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=aussie-author">aussie-author</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734021622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8418641936219221290">A powerful novel, set in Colombia, reliving the conflict of army vs guerilla vs drug lords, etc. You get the drift. It follows two and a half years of the life of child soldier Pedro, who is forced to watch the murder of his father at the hands of guerillas on his family farm, then, wracked with guilt, he enlists with terrorist organisation the Autodefencas to fight the guerillas when he is only fifteen.<br/><br/>We follow Pedro and his best friend Palillo as they go through their training, and start to r</span>
  <span id="freeText8418641936219221290" style="display:none">A powerful novel, set in Colombia, reliving the conflict of army vs guerilla vs drug lords, etc. You get the drift. It follows two and a half years of the life of child soldier Pedro, who is forced to watch the murder of his father at the hands of guerillas on his family farm, then, wracked with guilt, he enlists with terrorist organisation the Autodefencas to fight the guerillas when he is only fifteen.<br /><br />We follow Pedro and his best friend Palillo as they go through their training, and start to rise up the ranks of the organisation. We go on missions, watch with them in terror as they and their friends go through a living hell, we laugh, cry and love with these soldiers, often forgetting that they are only kids, as they are forced to grow up far too fast in a harsh regime.<br /><br />This is a hard book to put down, yet it is far from an easy read. Well researched and terrifyingly realistic, author Rusty Young has based his novel on the real stories of child soldiers he has met in Colombia. It's definitely not a book for a single sitting, the kindle edition clocking in at over 800 pages, but the time goes quickly as you find yourself totally absorbed in Pedro's story. It is a true eye-opener about current affairs we never truly appreciate are happening in our world. Highly recommended.<br /><br />My thanks to NetGalley and the publisher Havelock And Baker for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3172135060?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3172135060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10885387715009854725">This is a novel that I will remember but I will not reread it at any time in the future. I appreciate the Author's effort to present Columbia most complicated times under FARC. I followed the news regarding this organzation and the brutality of life under its terror, however, this novel opened my eyes to the crude reality that prevailed in those days and what impact it had on ordinary people. The novel tells a story of a boy, Pedro, who, seeking revenge for his father's murder turns into a cruel</span>
  <span id="freeText10885387715009854725" style="display:none">This is a novel that I will remember but I will not reread it at any time in the future. I appreciate the Author's effort to present Columbia most complicated times under FARC. I followed the news regarding this organzation and the brutality of life under its terror, however, this novel opened my eyes to the crude reality that prevailed in those days and what impact it had on ordinary people. The novel tells a story of a boy, Pedro, who, seeking revenge for his father's murder turns into a cruel man, like the man who killed his father. While half way through, I realized that cruelty and easiness to kill or lose one's life became so common that life itself had no value any more. At a certain point I did not expect anything else but more cruelty, and I was afraid it might not have any effect on me. And this was when I decided this book does not deliver .. A most terrifyng conclusion to a novel ... 'Colombiano' is an important witness to those times, but the novel is too long, and very much disturbing and upsetting.<br />*Many thank to Rusty Young, Havelock&amp;Baker Publishing and NetGalley for arc in exchange for my honest review.*</span>

<div id="review_2943502151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2943502151" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2943502151?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43861960-colombiano">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2943502151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16040325089277226501">Gritty, Raw, Powerful, Captivating, Thought provoking and gut wrenching.<br/><br/>What happens when you really don't have a choice? What happens when choices are made for you? What happens when your life changes in an instant? What happens when you make a simple decision and it changes your life and outlook.<br/><br/>Pedro GutiÃ©rrez is a happy teenager living in Columbia. He spends his days going to school, fishing, spending time with his best friend, Palillo and his girlfriend, Camilla. His world instantly changes</span>
  <span id="freeText16040325089277226501" style="display:none">Gritty, Raw, Powerful, Captivating, Thought provoking and gut wrenching.<br /><br />What happens when you really don't have a choice? What happens when choices are made for you? What happens when your life changes in an instant? What happens when you make a simple decision and it changes your life and outlook.<br /><br />Pedro GutiÃ©rrez is a happy teenager living in Columbia. He spends his days going to school, fishing, spending time with his best friend, Palillo and his girlfriend, Camilla. His world instantly changes when Guerrilla soldiers execute his father in front of him. Vowing vengeance, he goes on a journey that takes him from being a happy teen to a child soldier in a paramilitary group where he is trained to shot, fight and kill. Vengeance is always in his mind as he perfects his skills in hopes of tracking down the man who killed his father.<br /><br />It is safe to say that this is not your average coming of age story. There are parts (many) in this book that are quite gruesome but are important for the story as these things are real. Blending fact with fiction, this book looks at how child soldiers are trained, and used to fight battles over land territory, politics, cocaine, and power.<br /><br />How far will he go before he can say "vengeance is mine?" This is a HUGE book and at times it did feel it's size. But it also felt powerful, sad, realistic and shocking. It's sad to sit and think that there are child soldiers in many parts of the world who have lost their childhood and innocence for a life of violence. That there are places where a good man does what he feels in his heart is the right thing to do and pays for it with his life? This book is very realistic and visual. It is also well written, well thought out, perfectly paced and researched. This book took me though several feelings and emotions. <br /><br />This one was hard to put down and had my attention from the start. <br /><br />Thank you to Rusty Young, Lily from Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and NetGalley who provided me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All the thoughts and opinions are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16040325089277226501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15916384175219681100" style="display:none">Captivating from start to finish! <br />âThe war was like a slow burning campfire onto which both sides occasionally threw wood. And thatâs probably the way it wouldâve continued, if not for the arrival of the<br />Autodefensasâ. ( United Self-Defenders of Colombia).<br /><br />The campaign against organize crime in Columbia, has caused a violent response, increasing vulnerability of the civilian population due to the skirmishes between the organizations and the federal forces. <br /><br />Author Rusty Young, Australian born, was recruited as a Program Director of the U.S. Government anti-kidnapping program in Columbia. <br />It was so dangerous, that Rusty Young, had to keep his job completely secret from his family and friends. <br />Hate, violence, drugs, children soldiers, a divided country.....Columbia had the highest murder rate of journalists in the world. Rusty, himself wasnât a true journalist- but he might as well have been. He was working in a country with two terrorist organizations whose members numbered in the tens of thousands. <br />The first group was the FARC Guerrilla. Farmers aimed to fight poverty and social inequality by toppling the government and installing communist rule. To fund their revolution, they taxed businesses and kidnapped their rich, appropriating their lands for redistribution to the poor. <br />The second group - the Paramilitaries- was created in response. Wealthy land business owners, tired of the governments failure to protect them, formed their own private militias and âdeath squadsâ. <br /><br />Youngâs dedication to human rights - risking the safety of his own life - and the lives of others he interviewed - being in the heart of corruption and violent crimes - tells me that Rusty Young is one heck of an extraordinary human being....let alone an exciting storyteller. <br /><br />This story - fact and fiction IS GRIPPING - written in storytelling - dramatic- style. It reads like a thriller.....true crime suspense with frightening - complicated revenge, danger, betrayal, power struggles, cocaine, punishment, death, and eventually a form of redemption. <br /><br />The book begins when Pedro Gutierrez, the teenage adolescent narrator, was 15 years of age. <br />Pedroâs father was executed in front of him by Guerrilla soldiers. He and his mother were extradited from their farm. Pedro retaliates by joining an illegal paramilitary group with his close friend Palillo. <br /><br />Itâs a long book - but reads fast: Pedro, Palillo, and the other teens are brave in the face of unimaginable adversity. <br />Engrossing from the first page. Stunning story of strength and survival. It is sometimes brutal....but always fascinating. It shows terrorism at a shockingly personal level. <br /><br />âChild-soldiersâ....( two words that donât belong together), has always been unfathomable to me. But âColombiano â is a wrenching, and mesmerizing important story. <br />Rusty Young describes the unthinkable, and the unforgettable. <br /><br />Inspiring triumph....this book shines with energy - leaving a profound impression on the reader. I never - EVER- expected THIS BOOK - to be SUCH A PAGE TURNER....but anyone who starts it, is bound to have their own unputdownable experience. <br /><br />âCrouching in a ditch with Palillo, an hour before dawn, I realized my life was now divided in two. The time before Papa. And the time after. <br /> âMy dream of running the âfincaâ, ( Farm), with him and taking it over during his old age was shattered, and I replaced it with a far darker ambition: to track down and punish his murderersâ.<br /><br />Powerful as can be! <br />Many thanks to Lily at Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing with the advance gift of both the Audiobook and ebook. Listening to interviews with the author - enriched my admiration for Rusty Young. <br />Thanks again, Lily .....( Iâm genuinely glad I read this....I donât think Iâll ever be able to forget.<br /><br />Kudos to Rusty Young.....( mean guy...now I âmustâ read your first book, Marching Powderâ). I loved your interview talking about Bolivia, and your âREQUESTâ to stay in the San Pedro prison. Glad you never smuggled drugs in! Ha! <br /><br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11901882084683224768">This is a great big book. <br/><br/>But....<br/><br/>Is it a great-big book or a great big-book? That's debatable. <br/><br/>Despite the short chapters, it still reads like a great-big book which makes for a less than great big-book.<br/><br/>For me to really enjoy a great-big book I need to connect with the characters on a cellular level. I felt no investment in Pedro and his plight to avenge his father's murder and that disconnect lies solely in the lap of the authors inability to humanize this young character. <br/><br/>This is a fascinating</span>
  <span id="freeText11901882084683224768" style="display:none">This is a great big book. <br /><br />But....<br /><br />Is it a great-big book or a great big-book? That's debatable. <br /><br />Despite the short chapters, it still reads like a great-big book which makes for a less than great big-book.<br /><br />For me to really enjoy a great-big book I need to connect with the characters on a cellular level. I felt no investment in Pedro and his plight to avenge his father's murder and that disconnect lies solely in the lap of the authors inability to humanize this young character. <br /><br />This is a fascinating story with tremendous potential and I have no regrets investing my time to read it. But it felt more like a perfunctory lesson than epic storytelling. <br /><br />It's a good great-big book. <br /><br />3.5 Stars rounded up â­<br /><br /><br />** Thank you to Lily from Havelock and Baker Publishing for an ARC in exchange for an honest review. **</span>

<div id="review_3065748228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3065748228" />
    <a title="marilyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49815208-marilyn"><img alt="marilyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522535580p2/49815208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3065748228?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="marilyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="marilyn" href="/user/show/49815208-marilyn">marilyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780648445319" href="/book/show/48550704-colombiano">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49815208-marilyn?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49815208-marilyn?shelf=netgalley-2019">netgalley-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49815208-marilyn?shelf=traveling-friends-read">traveling-friends-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3065748228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7086640570393349516">This book was so far out of my comfort zone that I wasn't sure I should read it, but I'm so very glad I did. The author, Rusty Young, did an excellent job of making the character, Pedro, someone I cared about. I wanted to know what was going to happen to Pedro, his friends, family, and the other people in his life. <br/><br/>Until I read this book, then watched some videos and read other material, I had very little understanding about the massive use of children to fight civil wars in Columbia. This story</span>
  <span id="freeText7086640570393349516" style="display:none">This book was so far out of my comfort zone that I wasn't sure I should read it, but I'm so very glad I did. The author, Rusty Young, did an excellent job of making the character, Pedro, someone I cared about. I wanted to know what was going to happen to Pedro, his friends, family, and the other people in his life. <br /><br />Until I read this book, then watched some videos and read other material, I had very little understanding about the massive use of children to fight civil wars in Columbia. This story deals with two terrorist groups that use thousands of children to fight their wars, children that are forced to watch and participate in torture and murders. Once in these organizations, these children have no real hope of escaping, except by death. Everyday brings a new chance to watch those around them endure brutality or death by those who rule their lives. <br /><br />Men's lust for power and money drive these wars and cocaine fuels the war machine. Townsfolk live in poverty and fear as both sides reign terror on the people, sometimes pretending to protect or help them while really using humans as fodder for their greed and brutality. Once I started reading, I did not want to put this book down. Not only did I learn what might cause children to think their only hope might be to join a terrorist group, I also was able to see that possibly even the worst of the barbarian soldiers, once had to face such decisions, as children, to save their own lives or the lives of their families.<br /><br />Pedro and his mother and father live on their small farm and have managed to stay out of the fray as much as they can until finally Pedro and his dad anger one of the factions. Pedro's dad is murdered in front of Pedro and his mother and Pedro vows to kill the men who were involved in his father's death, the same men who forbid Pedro and his mother to bury his father or ever set foot on their farm again. Pedro joins the other terrorist group, which claims it's helping the people by fighting the guerrilla group. It's only later, once there is no turning back, that Pedro knows that he's trapped in a organization that is as brutal as the one that killed his father. Yet the desire for revenge keeps Pedro finding excuses to "soldier" on, often becoming what he hates most. <br /><br />This is such a heartrending story and it's based in fact. It's hard enough imagining grownups seeing and enduring such horrible cruelty but knowing that children are thrown into this world and expected to live and perpetuate more horror on others, is horrifying. How do they come back from this, if they ever have a chance to do so? <br /><br /> I want to thank NetGalley and Lily with Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing for providing this ARC to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7086640570393349516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

He was assisting the Colombian Government's anti terrorist operations. During this time he interviewed many former soldiers from FARC, the Communist guerrilla organization, and AUC, the right wing paramilitary organization. <br/>FARC has waged war against the government for 50 years or more. Both they and AUC draft child soldiers as young as 8 years old. The civil war is vicious and cruel. Both</span>
  <span id="freeText14118842855504708372" style="display:none">4 bright stars for a very long(819 pages) book. The author was an undercover agent for the U.S. Government. He was assisting the Colombian Government's anti terrorist operations. During this time he interviewed many former soldiers from FARC, the Communist guerrilla organization, and AUC, the right wing paramilitary organization. <br />FARC has waged war against the government for 50 years or more. Both they and AUC draft child soldiers as young as 8 years old. The civil war is vicious and cruel. Both sides use torture and profit from sale of narcotics.<br />The book is an autobiography of an ex AUC soldier whose name has been changed. It starts with Pedro joining the AUC after FARC murders his father in front of him. At the end of the book peace is declared by all sides. According to news stories, the peace has held up for several years, but FARC has recently complained of unfair treatment.<br />One quote by Pedro: "To someone who has not had a parent stolen from them, I can only attempt to explain how t feels. It's like having part of yourself hacked off without warning."<br />Thanks to Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing for sending me this eARC through NetGalley.</span>

<div id="review_3194182781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3194182781" />
    <a title="Sumit RK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38271102-sumit-rk"><img alt="Sumit RK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599896274p2/38271102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3194182781?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sumit RK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sumit RK" href="/user/show/38271102-sumit-rk">Sumit RK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3194182781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13723748937102520260"><br/><b>You have to pick a side. Or one will be picked for You. .</b><br/><br/>Set in Colombia, Colombiano is an epic story of revenge and vengeance. Blending fact and fiction, Colombiano narrates the story of a teenager Pedro GutiÃ©rrez whose life is ripped apart when Guerrilla soldiers callously execute his father in front of his eyes and he and his mother are banished from their farm. Swearing vengeance against the five men responsible, Pedro, with his best friend Palillo, joins an illegal Paramilitary group, where</span>
  <span id="freeText13723748937102520260" style="display:none"><br /><b>You have to pick a side. Or one will be picked for You. .</b><br /><br />Set in Colombia, Colombiano is an epic story of revenge and vengeance. Blending fact and fiction, Colombiano narrates the story of a teenager Pedro GutiÃ©rrez whose life is ripped apart when Guerrilla soldiers callously execute his father in front of his eyes and he and his mother are banished from their farm. Swearing vengeance against the five men responsible, Pedro, with his best friend Palillo, joins an illegal Paramilitary group, where he is trained to fight the guerrillas. Soon Pedro finds himself sinking deeper and deeper into Colombiaâs civil war and into a world of unspeakable violence. Pedro must now decide how far he is willing to go for vendetta. Can he stop himself before he becomes exactly what he despises? <br /><br />At the heart of the story, Colombiano is an epic tale of revenge of a boy set against the backdrop of a raging civil war. While the story explores in great detail, the war between the Colombian Govt, Autodefensas and the Guerrillas, Pedro remains at the center of the story always. We follow Pedro as he rises through the ranks, and fights in deadly missions, all the while with the turmoil in his personal life and planning to kill those who killed his father.<br /><br />Rusty Young has worked secretly for the US government in Colombia for four years and that shows in his research which is top-notch as well the characters he has created which all seem so real. The story has some excellent characters, particularly Pedro and his friends. We feel a part of them as they undergo brutal training, go on missions, we feel their happiness and sorrow as a part of the squad. <br /><br />At almost 700 pages, the book is long but the pace and the short chapters make it a fast read. There are parts of this book that are quite gruesome and the story does not gloss over the horrors of a full-blown civil war. From the training of child soldiers to torture and body mutilation, the violence in this book is raw and hard to read at times. I felt the book focused too much on the character backstories and Pedroâs personal revenge. The story could have focused on the bigger story of civil war instead. Having said that, Pedroâs personal journey from seeking revenge to slowly realizing the futility of it all is an incredible journey and which makes the book immensely readable. <br /><br /><br />Overall, Colombiano is a well-researched and chillingly realistic insight into the civil war in Colombia. It is well written, perfectly paced and if you enjoy reading action thrillers, you should absolutely read this. <br /><br /><b> Many thanks to the publishers Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and Netgalley for the ARC. </b>â<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13723748937102520260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8897170668625988687">Colombiano by Rusty Young is a story you will not soon forget. This is a work of fiction though the horrors of the Colombian civil war and its aftermath are part of history. The author worked in Colombia with the Anti-Kidnapping Program in a country that averaged eight kidnappings per day. While in-country, he interviewed the child soldiers on both sides of the war and these are the basis of this novel. Pedro, a fifteen-year-old boy, witnessed the execution of his father, by guerillas. He was ex</span>
  <span id="freeText8897170668625988687" style="display:none">Colombiano by Rusty Young is a story you will not soon forget. This is a work of fiction though the horrors of the Colombian civil war and its aftermath are part of history. The author worked in Colombia with the Anti-Kidnapping Program in a country that averaged eight kidnappings per day. While in-country, he interviewed the child soldiers on both sides of the war and these are the basis of this novel. Pedro, a fifteen-year-old boy, witnessed the execution of his father, by guerillas. He was executed for allegedly providing drinking water to their enemies. They then banned Pedro and his mother from their farm. The boy vowed to avenge his fatherâs death and joined and was trained by the paramilitaries. Brutality became part of his daily existence. This is a story of revenge and a story of children fighting a war. I admit that I skipped some passages due to the graphic violence but this is a book that needed to be written and needs to be read. Thank you to Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and NetGalley for the e-ARC in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2979733993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2979733993" />
    <a title="Andy Marr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8228243-andy-marr"><img alt="Andy Marr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602706259p2/8228243.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2979733993?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Marr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Marr" href="/user/show/8228243-andy-marr">Andy Marr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2979733993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17542599412028462826">For the most part, this fact-meets-fiction account of the civil war between the army and opposing Guerrilla forces in 21st-century Colombia, and particularly the role of child soldiers in the conflict, was a powerful and well-written book. With its themes of loss, revenge, cruelty, betrayal and corruption, it kept my attention from start to finish, which is no mean feat for a story that runs to almost 700 pages. In fact, I feel almost guilty giving the book only 4 stars, but a few elements preve</span>
  <span id="freeText17542599412028462826" style="display:none">For the most part, this fact-meets-fiction account of the civil war between the army and opposing Guerrilla forces in 21st-century Colombia, and particularly the role of child soldiers in the conflict, was a powerful and well-written book. With its themes of loss, revenge, cruelty, betrayal and corruption, it kept my attention from start to finish, which is no mean feat for a story that runs to almost 700 pages. In fact, I feel almost guilty giving the book only 4 stars, but a few elements prevented me from giving it full marks.<br /><br />First, the spoilers. For example, the novel began by telling us that Pablo's father was shot by the Guerrilla. This was all very well, except that the killing didn't take place until around page 40. So, later on, when the father was on his knees, the Guerrilla circling him with a gun in his hand, we already knew what was going to happen and the tension was lost completely. <br /><br />Second, the length. Although the story was well told, I do feel that the novel would have benefited from another careful edit. I think that 150-200 pages could easily have been cut from the book without the story-line being affected. In fact, by condensing or taking out sections where the novel began to drag - for example, during Pablo's first attempt to assassinate Raton - the story would only have become more gripping.<br /><br />Third, the dialogue. This could definitely have been improved upon, especially during the more romantic scenes between Pablo and his girlfriend. At times, when things got particularly smoochy between the two, the writing became almost unbearably cheesy. I'd quote a couple of examples here, but - honestly - I'd probably get a bit sick in my mouth just by typing them out.<br /><br />Despite these obvious faults, Colombiano was a good read and I'd happily recommend it, particularly to fans of crime, action and adventure novels.<br /><br />*** Thank you to the publisher for the ARC provided in exchange for an honest opinion. ***</span>
  <a data-text-id="17542599412028462826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2977748592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2977748592" />
    <a title="Ujjawal Sureka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89336018-ujjawal-sureka"><img alt="Ujjawal Sureka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589457921p2/89336018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2977748592?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ujjawal Sureka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ujjawal Sureka" href="/user/show/89336018-ujjawal-sureka">Ujjawal Sureka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89336018-ujjawal-sureka?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2977748592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1889078679431758513"><b>Genre</b>: Biography, War, Terrorism, Violence, Morality.<br/><b>Publication Date</b>: August 2017<br/><br/>The book is captivating at first glance. The terrorist atmosphere of Columbia has always been fascinating, with people(children and adult alike) being at constant warfare and fighting to live another day. <br/><br/>The strory revolves around the lead, Pedro Gutierrez, an innocent child, who's happy and fun life is turned 180 when his religious and peace loving father is killed by a group of terrorists. In the immediate fit o</span>
  <span id="freeText1889078679431758513" style="display:none"><b>Genre</b>: Biography, War, Terrorism, Violence, Morality.<br /><b>Publication Date</b>: August 2017<br /><br />The book is captivating at first glance. The terrorist atmosphere of Columbia has always been fascinating, with people(children and adult alike) being at constant warfare and fighting to live another day. <br /><br />The strory revolves around the lead, Pedro Gutierrez, an innocent child, who's happy and fun life is turned 180 when his religious and peace loving father is killed by a group of terrorists. In the immediate fit of rage he leaves everything behind to become able to kill his father's killers. In this pursuit he is faced with choices, many heroic and many filled with pain and agony. Will he be able to serve justice? or will he forget his roots in the frenzy of war? <br /><br />The story(a mix of fact and fiction) is intense and captivating. The writing is brilliant and encaptures a range of emotions. At times its tough to put the book/kindle down, inspite of not liking the things we just read.<br /><br />The military feel is real. The training, the punishments, the planning, the attention to detail, the war, the chaos and the blood shed. It was like a movie playing in front of me. It does remind me of Narcos.<br /><br />The storyline is very engaging and sometimes I find myself completely engrossed in it. Both the writing and the story have a sense originality in them and it only gets better as it progresses.<br /><br />Some of the scenes can make our hearts ache, we may empathize and sympathize, but we civilians can never know what the people involved in war go through. The author also brings in the touch of morality and how one perceives the same thing much differently than the other. With all its heartaches and surprises, I loved this book.<br /><br />P.S: Thanks to Lily from Havelock and Baker Publishing and the Publishing team for giving me a copy in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1889078679431758513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3071858722" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10846058051586991739">â...what sort of justice can exist in such a corrupt, hypocritical system?â <br/><br/>5 stunningly powerful stars!<br/><br/>Tension-filled. Eye-opening. Pulse-pounding. Suspenseful. Gut-wrenching. Unforgettable. <br/><br/>Growing up in Colombia, Pedro is only fifteen years old when he is forced to watch guerrilla soldiers execute his father. Vowing to seek revenge, he joins the Paramilitaries where he spends the next two and a half years hunting his fathers killers. Based on Pedroâs real life story, this book details the tor</span>
  <span id="freeText10846058051586991739" style="display:none">â...what sort of justice can exist in such a corrupt, hypocritical system?â <br /><br />5 stunningly powerful stars!<br /><br />Tension-filled. Eye-opening. Pulse-pounding. Suspenseful. Gut-wrenching. Unforgettable. <br /><br />Growing up in Colombia, Pedro is only fifteen years old when he is forced to watch guerrilla soldiers execute his father. Vowing to seek revenge, he joins the Paramilitaries where he spends the next two and a half years hunting his fathers killers. Based on Pedroâs real life story, this book details the torturous training, brutal violence and gruesome brainwashing that is forced upon these child soldiers.<br /><br />Pedro was a character I connected with immediately and felt completely invested in on each and every one of the 689 pages. This book took me longer than usual to finish, not because it didnât keep my attention, but because it affected me so deeply that I had to take breaks from it to calm myself down and accept what was happening to Pedro. His story is not an easy one to read. It will break your heart and frustrate you. It will give you hope, only to have you turn the page and find that hope being stomped on and buried deep in the ground. <br /><br />There are endless powerful words I could use to describe this book. It is truly one I will never forget reading. I applaud the author, Rusty Young, for writing this outstanding story. Rusty is a brave journalist who lives in Colombia and has first hand experience with many rescued child soldiers going through rehabilitation. He gave a voice to Pedro which represents the voices of countless child soldiers who have faced the atrocities that are described within these pages. A truly powerful and important read that I highly recommend!<br /><br />Thank you to Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing for sending me a physical copy! This is a book I wouldnât have picked up on my own. Thank you for taking me outside of my comfort zone and giving me the opportunity to read Pedroâs unforgettable story.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3839279166393166427">You canât truly know what someone else is going through without walking in his shoes. Unless Mr. Young writes about it. In Colombiano, those of us fortunate enough to be far removed from any war zone, see exactly what living amid battles entails; in day-to-day life, as well the overall impact it has on absolutely everything.<br/><br/>Certainly, most people know that the Guerilla evoke evil with their aggressive cocaine manufacturing and distribution. The gross misunderstanding is that the Guerilla are fig</span>
  <span id="freeText3839279166393166427" style="display:none">You canât truly know what someone else is going through without walking in his shoes. Unless Mr. Young writes about it. In Colombiano, those of us fortunate enough to be far removed from any war zone, see exactly what living amid battles entails; in day-to-day life, as well the overall impact it has on absolutely everything.<br /><br />Certainly, most people know that the Guerilla evoke evil with their aggressive cocaine manufacturing and distribution. The gross misunderstanding is that the Guerilla are fighting the army and law enforcement; not citizens. Leading to the false conclusion that, if folks go about their business, thereâs no real reason for this pesky fighting to bother them. The carefully controlled propaganda supports this theory. Even having the place of worship utterly obliterated by âerrantâ fire is only an unfortunate consequence.<br /><br />Pedro has listened to placates until he thought his head may explode. Papi made sure he contained, or at least properly channeled, his rage. There was Camila to consider. Rounding out the small group of people close to Pedro is the somewhat goofy, undeniably adorable, Pallilo. Pedro can push his anger aside for them.<br /><br />Right up until the Guerilla descended on his fatherâs farm. In front of his disbelieving eyes, Papi is surrounded as accusations are hurled. The feisty fifteen-year-old cannot watch the depraved tirade and hold his tongue. Boldly, stupidly, Pedro demands an explanation. His fatherâs crime was revealed with a hint of glee. The farmer had the audacity to allow soldiers from the army to drink water from his well. <br /><br />The resulting punishment is a defining, dividing moment for Pedro. There are men like Papi. Those who believed, as people of God, it was never right to deny a thirsty man a drink. And there are monsters masquerading as menâthe Guerilla.<br /><br />The situation that Pedro is forced to face is tragic. His retaliatory actions, atrocious. And yetâ¦the author manages to demonstrate how a furious and yes, frightened, adolescent can morph into a ruthless man-killerâall the while reminding the reader that Pedro remains, essentially, a boy. <br /><br />This review was written by jv poore for Buried Under Books, with huge thanks to Havelock and Baker Publishing for the Advance Review Copy to be donated to my favorite classroom library.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2940550528?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2940550528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3594583494551784978">Colombiano is an account of the horrific violence endured by the citizens of Colombia in their decades old civil war fought between the government and the socialist terrorist organization FARC. There are paramilitary groups also involved who are supposedly on the side of the government, but are really just another set of terrorists, as illustrated by this novel.<br/><br/>A young boy named Pedro is the main character, who having watched his father be executed by FARC, determines to kill the men who did it.</span>
  <span id="freeText3594583494551784978" style="display:none">Colombiano is an account of the horrific violence endured by the citizens of Colombia in their decades old civil war fought between the government and the socialist terrorist organization FARC. There are paramilitary groups also involved who are supposedly on the side of the government, but are really just another set of terrorists, as illustrated by this novel.<br /><br />A young boy named Pedro is the main character, who having watched his father be executed by FARC, determines to kill the men who did it. He joins a paramilitary group and goes through the brutal and gruesome indoctrination that desensitizes him to torture and murder. Starting at age 15 until 18 we witness his corruption as he becomes like the men who his father despised. <br /><br />This is an interesting and action packed read, but I felt it was too long and a bit repetitive. The ending was particularly torturous, as the author tacks on so much follow up, it becomes anti-climatic. <br /><br />I received a copy of this book from Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and NetGalley in exchange for an open and honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2934453026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2934453026" />
    <a title="Nadia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57073687-nadia"><img alt="Nadia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512742969p2/57073687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2934453026?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadia" href="/user/show/57073687-nadia">Nadia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57073687-nadia?shelf=best-of-2019">best-of-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57073687-nadia?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2934453026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1614809011929504127">There are books I loved, but forgot about them in a few weeks. And then there are books I loved and won't be able to forget for a long time. Colombiano definitely belongs to the latter category. Even though it is a work of fiction, it is based on a true conflict in Colombia between the comunist Guerillas and opposing Paramilitaries. The author interviewed numerous former child soldiers whose tragic stories are told in the book.<br/><br/>Pedro is a 15 year old boy who lives on a farm in Llorona, Colombia, </span>
  <span id="freeText1614809011929504127" style="display:none">There are books I loved, but forgot about them in a few weeks. And then there are books I loved and won't be able to forget for a long time. Colombiano definitely belongs to the latter category. Even though it is a work of fiction, it is based on a true conflict in Colombia between the comunist Guerillas and opposing Paramilitaries. The author interviewed numerous former child soldiers whose tragic stories are told in the book.<br /><br />Pedro is a 15 year old boy who lives on a farm in Llorona, Colombia, with his father and mother. Pedro has a simple but happy life and spends most of his time with his beutiful girlfriend Camilla and his best friend Palillo. Everything changes for Pedro one Wednesday morning when the Guerillas come to Pedro's parents farm and kill Pedro's father. The 15 year old carefree boy has no choice other than to grow up overnight to take care of his mother. Hurting and grieving Pedro swears to kill all the Guerilla's who participated in his father's killing. To achieve his revenge Pedro and Palillo join the paramilitaries and start training to become soldiers.<br /><br />Told from Pedro's point of view, Colombiano is an unforgettable story of a young boy's transformation of becoming a teen soldier in order to avenge his father's murder. I'm personally an emotional reader and connecting with the main character is vital for me. Connecting with Pedro couldn't have been easier and I was fully invested in his story. Pedro's pain from losing his beloved father was palpable and I didn't doubt for a second that he was going to track down his killers as he set himself to do.<br /><br />Powerful, gritty and raw, Colombiano provides an uncompromising look at the war conflict, corruption and drug-trafficking in Colombia via a tragic and intense story of a young boy. This must be one of my best reads in 2019.<br /><br /><i>Many thanks to Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing for my copy of the book in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1614809011929504127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2927048035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2927048035" />
    <a title="Paige" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99327714-paige"><img alt="Paige" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572539777p2/99327714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2927048035?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paige" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paige" href="/user/show/99327714-paige">Paige</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43861960-colombiano">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99327714-paige?shelf=cultural">cultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99327714-paige?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2927048035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9126563994612936091">Based on true events, this story of revenge, betrayal, and corruption follows the fictional character Pedro. Growing up in Llorona, a war-torn land who makes good on the promise to kill those who snitch, Pedro witnesses the murder of his father. At fifteen years old, going on sixteen, he joins the Autodefensas in order to extract revenge on the Guerillas who killed his father. However, his alliance with the Autodefensas creates conflicts in his relationships. <i>It truly is a great story with remar</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9126563994612936091" style="display:none">Based on true events, this story of revenge, betrayal, and corruption follows the fictional character Pedro. Growing up in Llorona, a war-torn land who makes good on the promise to kill those who snitch, Pedro witnesses the murder of his father. At fifteen years old, going on sixteen, he joins the Autodefensas in order to extract revenge on the Guerillas who killed his father. However, his alliance with the Autodefensas creates conflicts in his relationships. <i>It truly is a great story with remarkable characters that endured so much. From the drug trafficking to the kidnappings, I really enjoyed it.</i><br /><br /><b>Now, to my technical details!</b> Early on his father is killed and Pedro vows to kill each man who took part in his fatherâs murder. After this occurs and he joins the paramilitary, Pedroâs training with the Autodefensas is detailed until 24% (on a Kindle). <b>That leaves 25%-97% being the tale of a teenage boy carrying out revenge.</b> It is an 800+ page book, so this was a very drawn-out revenge. It just kept going and going with him trying to find the next person who was involved in his father's murder, and I took off an entire star because of it. At a certain point (55% for those interested) I wanted the revenge to be over and the story to progress, but Pedro still had more revenge to pursue. Though entertaining and a powerful story, this left me feeling winded as a reader. <br /><br />It was full of thoughtful and meaningful prose which caused me to highlight a lot. It has a lot of violence and vulgar content, too: scenes with dead body parts floating in the water, boys calling each other s.o.bâs every few pages, etc. There are a few sex scenes, but the sexy details are not included. <br /> <br />There are many Spanish words, but most are cognates. However, if you are unfamiliar with basic Spanish words then I recommend reading on a Kindle in order to translate. There is a glossary of Spanish terms at the end, but that seems superfluous to have to flip back and forth, but do you boo.<br /><br /><i>I recommend this book to lovers of historical fiction and those with multicultural interests.</i> <b>Overall, a great compelling read about a boy soldier in Colombia with many well-researched details. </b> Many thanks to Lily Green at Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing for this copy. All opinions are my own.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3055174967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10451237491693757379"><br/><b>***most deserving 5 star rating I have ever given***</b><br/><br/> <blockquote>
  <i>"Nevertheless, right then and there, I resolved that one day I'd tell my life story to someone who would be willing to publish it. I know I've done terrible things - killed people and even worse. I know I've lied to those I love. But people need to know that this is not a lie. The things I've witnessed with these eyes - these stories I'm telling you - they're too horrible for anyone to invent. This is the truth about Colombia and I want peo</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10451237491693757379" style="display:none"><br /><b>***most deserving 5 star rating I have ever given***</b><br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>"Nevertheless, right then and there, I resolved that one day I'd tell my life story to someone who would be willing to publish it. I know I've done terrible things - killed people and even worse. I know I've lied to those I love. But people need to know that this is not a lie. The things I've witnessed with these eyes - these stories I'm telling you - they're too horrible for anyone to invent. This is the truth about Colombia and I want people to know it." </i>
</blockquote><br />I donât know if there is anything I can say about this book that would do it justice. It's been well over a day since I finished reading it and I still can barely put into words how amazing it is! Probably the best book I've read in I don't know how long and a story that will stay with me to the end of times.<br /><br />Colombiano is the powerful tale of a fifteen year old boy named Pedro, who joins an illegal paramilitary group after he was forced to watch his father being brutally murdered right in front of him by the FARC guerrilla. As if this wasn't the worst thing that could happen to him, he and his mother are also banished from their family's farm. Furious and overcome with grief, he vows to find and punish the men responsible.<br /><br />As the story goes on, Pedro spirals deep into a world of unspeakable violence. Having already murdered two of the men responsible for his father's death, he finds himself at a crossroads - can he stop himself before he becomes just like the ones he is hunting or will he let his obsession with revenge take everything all he has left?<br /><br />I started reading this book in November last year and only finished it the other day, but not for a lack of trying or because it isn't good. <br /><br /><b>It is haunting. <br />It is gripping and poignant. <br />It is destined to provoke, enlighten and it's just so utterly captivating.</b><br /><br />But it's 689 pages long and I couldn't always find the right times to read it. As a matter of fact, I am actually glad I took my time to enjoy it, because this way I could let each chapter sink in, rather than just taking too much in at once.<br /><br />Colombiano is not only a gripping coming of age novel, it offers a glimpse into a dark side of Colombia's history, while also showing the redeeming power of love. I want to say more about the plot because there is SO much going on, but I also don't want to spoil anything for any future readers. That is why I'll stop here. <br /><br />But one more thing: if you get the chance <b>READ. THIS. BOOK.</b>!!!<br /><br /><i>***Thanks to Lily Green at Havelock &amp; Baker Publishing and to NetGalley, who provided me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.***</i></span>
